باب بيان تقسيم الناسخ
الحجج أربع : الكتاب والسنة، والإجماع، والقياس.
أما القياس: فلا يصلح ناسخاً؛ لما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
وأما الإجماع: فقد ذكر بعض المتأخرين أنه يصح النسخ به، والصحيح أن النسخ به لا يكون لأن النسخ لا يكون إلا في حياة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. والإجماع ليس بحجة في حياته صلى الله عليه وسلم؛ لأنه لا إجماع دون رأيه، والرجوع إليه فرض، وإذا وجد منه البيان: كان منفرداً بذلك، لا محالة، وإذا صار الإجماع واجب العمل به: لم يبق النسخ مشروعاً بعده. وإنما يجوز النسخ بالكتاب والسنة، وذلك أربعة أقسام:
١ - نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب.
٢- والسنة بالسنة.
٣- ونَسْخُ السنة بالكتاب.
٤ - ونَسْخُ الكتاب بالسنة.
وذلك كله جائز عندنا.
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله بفساد القسمين الأخيرين.
واحتج بقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا نَنسَحْ مِنْ ءَايَةٍ أَوْ نُنسِهَا نَأْتِ بِخَيْرٍ مِّنْهَا أَوْ مِثْلِهَا ﴾ البقرة / ١٠٦ ، وذلك بين الآيتين، والسنتين. فأما في القسمين الأخيرين : فلا.
واحتج أيضاً بقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا يَكُونُ لِي أَنْ أُبَدِّلَهُ مِن تِلْقَاي نَفْسِي﴾ يونس / ١٥ ، فثبت أن السنة لا تنسخ الكتاب.
واحتج بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا روي لكم عني حديث: فاعرضوه على كتاب الله تعالى : فإن وافق الكتاب فاقبلوه، وإن خالف فردوه» (١)
ولأن في هذا صيانة الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم عن شبهة الطعن ؛ لأنه لو نُسخ القرآن به أو سنته نُسخت بالكتاب : لكان مَدرَجةً إلى الطعن، فكان التعاون به أولى.
وقد احتج بعض أصحابنا رحمهم الله في ذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿ كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالأَقْرَبِينَ﴾ البقرة / ۱۸۰ : في الآية فَرْضُ هذه الوصية، ثم نسخت بقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا وصية لوارث» (۲)
Chapter: Statement of the Division of the Abrogator. The proofs are four: the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. As for analogy: it is not valid as an abrogator; as we will explain, God willing. As for consensus: some later scholars mentioned that abrogation by it is valid. The correct view is that abrogation by it cannot occur because abrogation only takes place during the lifetime of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Consensus is not a proof during his lifetime, peace be upon him; because there is no consensus without his opinion, and referring to him is obligatory. When he issues a clarification, he is alone in that, inevitably. And when consensus becomes binding to act upon, abrogation is no longer legislated after it. Abrogation is only permissible by the Book and the Sunnah, and that is four categories: 1. Abrogation of the Book by the Book. 2. Abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah. 3. Abrogation of the Sunnah by the Book. 4. Abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah. And all that is permissible in our view. Al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, declared the last two categories invalid. He argued with God's saying: 'Whatever verse We abrogate or cause to be forgotten, We bring one better than it or similar to it' [al-Baqarah 2:106], and that is between two verses and two Sunnahs. As for the last two categories: no. He also argued with God's saying: 'Say: It is not for me to change it of my own accord' [Yunus 10:15], so it is established that the Sunnah does not abrogate the Book. He also argued with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'If a hadith is narrated to you from me, present it to the Book of God: if it agrees with the Book, accept it; if it contradicts it, reject it.' And because in this is protection of the Messenger, peace be upon him, from the suspicion of criticism; because if the Quran were abrogated by it (i.e., Sunnah) or his Sunnah were abrogated by the Book, it would be a path to criticism, so cooperation in it is better. Some of our associates, may God have mercy on them, argued in that with God's saying: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, is to make a bequest for the parents and the near relatives' [al-Baqarah 2:180]: in this verse, this bequest is prescribed, then it was abrogated by the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'No bequest to an heir.'
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on the division of abrogation (naskh). The author begins by listing the four proofs of Islamic law: Quran, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). He then rules out qiyas as an abrogator, a point he promises to explain later. For ijma', he notes that some later scholars allowed naskh by ijma', but the correct Hanafi position is that abrogation cannot occur by ijma' because naskh only took place during the Prophet's lifetime, and ijma' was not a binding proof then (since the Prophet's opinion was authoritative). After his death, once ijma' becomes binding, no further abrogation is possible. Thus, naskh is limited to Quran and Sunnah, yielding four types: (1) Quran by Quran, (2) Sunnah by Sunnah, (3) Sunnah by Quran, and (4) Quran by Sunnah. The Hanafi school deems all four permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i rejects the last two (Sunnah abrogating Quran and vice versa). His proofs: (a) Verse 2:106 speaks of replacing a verse with a better or similar one, which he restricts to between two Quranic verses or two sunnahs. (b) Verse 10:15 indicates the Prophet does not change revelation on his own, denying Sunnah's ability to abrogate Quran. (c) A hadith instructs that reports contradicting the Quran should be rejected, implying Sunnah cannot abrogate Quran. (d) A rational argument: allowing inter-abrogation could lead to criticism of the Prophet. The Hanafi response, cited from some Hanafi scholars, uses the case of inheritance: the Quranic command for bequest to parents and relatives (2:180) was abrogated by the Prophet's hadith 'No bequest to an heir'—a clear example of Sunnah abrogating Quran. This demonstrates the practical occurrence of such naskh, supporting the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ناسخ (nāsikh): That which abrogates; the abrogating text or evidence.
منسوخ (mansūkh): The abrogated ruling or text.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; a method of deriving rulings from established principles.
إجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the scholars of the community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid example of abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah?
A) The verse of bequest (2:180) abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir'
B) The verse of stoning abrogated by the verse of flogging
C) The hadith about presenting to Quran abrogating all contradictory hadiths
D) The consensus of the Companions abrogating the verse of bequest

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits all four types of naskh between Quran and Sunnah, supported by the example of the bequest verse abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir'.

Abrogation of the Bequest Verse: Sunnah vs. Quran
Refuting the proof that a hadith abrogated the bequest verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether Sunnah can abrogate Quran and evaluate the proof that the bequest verse was abrogated by hadith.

Core Idea
The bequest verse was abrogated by Quran, not by hadith — Sunnah cannot directly abrogate the Quran.

This passage tackles a critical usul al-fiqh question: can the Sunnah abrogate the Quran? The opposing view is examined through the case of the bequest verse (2:180) allegedly abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir'. You will see how the Hanafi school upholds the principle that only Quran can abrogate Quran, and that the hadith merely confirms the abrogation already present in the inheritance verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its proof
Locate where some Hanafis argue that the bequest verse was abrogated by the hadith. What is their evidence?
The claim: the hadith 'No bequest to an heir' directly abrogated 2:180.
2
Examine the general arguments against Sunnah abrogating Quran
The author first presents three proofs that Sunnah cannot abrogate Quran: Quran 2:106 (naskh between like types), Quran 10:15 (Prophet cannot change Quran), and a hadith commanding presentation to Quran.
These are the pre-emptive dalil for the Hanafi position.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the bequest claim
The author gives two reasons why the bequest verse was abrogated by the Quran, not the hadith. First: the Quranic inheritance verses (4:11) made the bequest indefinite. Second: the hadith only confirms the abrogation.
The key distinction is between abrogator and evidence of abrogation.
4
Distinguish direct abrogation from supporting confirmation
Understand that the hadith does not remove the ruling; the Quran does. The hadith is evidence that the removal has already occurred, not the agent.
This preserves the principle of naskh between like types.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does it make? If the hadith were the abrogator, it would break the rule that Sunnah cannot abrogate Quran. If the Quran abrogated, the rule stands.
The dispute impacts the hierarchy of sources in usul.

وافق الكتاب فاقبلوه، وإن خالف فاردوه». ولأن في هذا صيانة الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم عن شبهة الطعن ؛ لأنه لو نُسخ القرآن به أو سنته نُسخت بالكتاب : لكان مَدرَجةً إلى الطعن، فكان التعاون به أولى. وقد الوصية، ثم نسخت بقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «فلا وصية لوارث». وهذا الاستدلال غير صحيح؛ لوجهين : أحدهما : أن النسخ إنما ثبت بآية المواريث، وبيانه: أنه قال تعالى : ﴿وَمِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي للقيد، كما يكون القيد نسخاً للإطلاق. والثاني : أن النسخ نوعان: أحدهما: ابتداء بعد انتهاء محض. كتفي، فسمعته يقول: «إن الله قد أعطى كل ذي حق حقه، فلا وصية لوارث». رواه الخمسة إلا أبا داود وصححه الترمذي الكامل، بسند فيه ضعف. وأخرجه ابن أبي شيبة موقوفاً، وهو أقوى، وحديث معقل بن يسار أخرجه ابن عدي وسنده واه وحديث خارجة بن عمرو أخرجه الطبراني، وجوز أبو موسى في الذيل أن يكون هذا هو عمرو بن خارجة. ومن ذلك : مرسل مجاهد، أخرجه البيهقي من طريق الشافعي، ومرسل عطاء وعمرو بن دينار وأبي جعفر الباقر، أخرجها الدارقطني، والله أعلم.
He argued with His statement: 'Whatever verse We abrogate or cause to be forgotten, We bring a better one or the like thereof' (Al-Baqarah 2:106) – that is between two verses or two Sunnahs. As for the last two categories, no. He also argued with His statement: 'Say, It is not for me to change it of my own accord' (Yunus 10:15). So it is established that the Sunnah does not abrogate the Book. And he argued with his saying, peace be upon him: 'If a hadith is narrated to you from me, present it to the Book of Allah: if it agrees with the Book, accept it; if it contradicts, reject it.' And because in this is protection of the Messenger, peace be upon him, from the suspicion of criticism; for if the Quran were abrogated by it, or his Sunnah were abrogated by the Book, it would be a path to criticism, so cooperation with it is more appropriate. And some of our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, argued in that regard with His statement: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, is the bequest for parents and near relatives' (Al-Baqarah 2:180) – in the verse is the obligation of this bequest, then it was abrogated by the Prophet's saying, peace be upon him: 'No bequest to an heir.' This reasoning is incorrect for two reasons: First: The abrogation is only established by the verses of inheritance; its explanation: He said: 'After a bequest they bequeath or a debt' (An-Nisa 4:11). So He made inheritance dependent on an indefinite bequest, while the first bequest was definite. So if that bequest remained with inheritance, then was abrogated by the Sunnah, it would necessitate that it be arranged upon the definite, so the absolute became an abrogation of the restricted, just as the restricted becomes an abrogation of the absolute. Second: Abrogation is of two types: one: beginning after pure cessation. ... 'Indeed Allah has given every rightful person his right, so no bequest to an heir.' Reported by the five except Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi authenticated it, and reported by the five except al-Nisa'i from the hadith of Abu Umamah, and al-Daraqutni from the hadith of Ibn Abbas similarly. The commentator said: This hadith is in the strength of mutawatir. I said: So let us mention what is easy for us of it: among that is the hadith of Amr, the hadith of Abu Umamah al-Bahili, the hadith of Ibn Abbas previously, the hadith of Ibn Amr reported by al-Daraqutni and Ibn Adi from Habib al-Muallim from Amr ibn Shuayb from his father from his grandfather, and its chain is good; the hadith of Anas reported by Ibn Majah, and its chain is good; the hadith of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, reported by Ibn Adi in al-Kamil, with a chain containing weakness; and it was reported by Ibn Abi Shayba as mauquf, which is stronger; the hadith of Maqil ibn Yasar reported by Ibn Adi with a weak chain; the hadith of Kharija ibn Amr reported by al-Tabarani, and Abu Musa in al-Dhayl considered that this might be Amr ibn Kharija. Among that: the mursal of Mujahid, reported by al-Bayhaqi via al-Shafi'i, and the mursal of Ata, Amr ibn Dinar, and Abu Jafar al-Baqir, reported by al-Daraqutni. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a detailed naskh analysis examining the claim that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran, specifically through the example of the bequest verse (2:180) allegedly abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir.' The author first presents the proofs of those who deny that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran (using Quran 2:106, 10:15, and the hadith about presenting hadith to the Quran). Then he mentions that some Hanafis used the bequest verse and its abrogation by the hadith as evidence that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran. The author refutes this by two arguments: (1) The abrogation actually occurred through the Quranic verses of inheritance (4:11), which replace the definite bequest with an indefinite one, effectively abrogating the specific bequest obligation. This is an abrogation of a restricted ruling by an absolute one, which is a valid type of naskh. (2) The hadith is support, but the real abrogating text is the Quran. The author then notes that the hadith is mutawatir in strength and lists its multiple chains. Thus, the passage upholds the principle that the Sunnah does not abrogate the Quran directly; rather, the Quran abrogates itself.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation, replacing it with another.
وصية (wasiyya): Bequest: a testamentary disposition of property to specified heirs.
مطلق (mutlaq): An unqualified or absolute term that applies universally without restriction.
مقيد (muqayyad): A restricted or qualified term that limits application to a specific condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the author, what is the first reason the argument that the bequest verse was abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir' is incorrect?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot abrogate the Quran.
B) The verse was actually abrogated by the Quranic inheritance verses (4:11), not by the hadith.
C) The bequest verse was never obligatory; it was always recommended.
D) The hadith is mutawatir and thus abrogates the verse directly.

Key Takeaway
The bequest verse was abrogated by Quranic inheritance verses, not by the hadith; thus, the principle that Sunnah cannot abrogate the Quran remains intact.

Naskh of Bequest for Heirs as Tahwil
Debating the nature of naskh regarding bequest for heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between absolute naskh and naskh by conversion (tahwil) and apply this distinction to the evolution of the bequest ruling for heirs.

Core Idea
Naskh can transform a ruling without annulling it entirely — bequest for heirs was converted into fixed inheritance.

In this passage, the author defends the Hanafi position that the abrogation of the bequest for heirs is not an outright cancellation but a conversion into the fixed inheritance system. This distinction is crucial for understanding how divine legislation can shift obligations without erasing the underlying purpose. The argument relies on the wording of the inheritance verse and the classification of naskh into two types, with the second exemplified by the change of qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
The text begins by rejecting an opponent's inference. Pinpoint what the opponent asserted about the naskh of the bequest for heirs.
The opponent likely argued for absolute naskh—complete annulment.
2
Analyze the first reason: linguistic evidence
The author uses the indefinite word 'وصية' in the inheritance verse to argue that the previously definite bequest was abrogated. Trace how the shift from definite to indefinite implies naskh.
This is a classic usul move: the absolute (mutlaq) abrogates the restricted (muqayyad) because the later text can override the earlier.
3
Examine the second reason: typology of naskh
The author states that naskh has two types: absolute and by conversion. Understand the analogy with the change of qibla to see how a ruling can be transformed rather than erased.
Tahwil preserves the obligation's essence while changing its form.
4
Evaluate the supporting evidence for the hadith
The author cites multiple narrations of 'لا وصية لوارث' to establish its strength, even arguing it reaches the level of mutawatir. Assess how this hadith supports the claim of naskh by conversion.
The hadith is used to confirm that after the inheritance verses, the earlier bequest ruling was replaced.

وهذا الاستدلال غير صحيح؛ لوجهين :
أحدهما : أن النسخ إنما ثبت بآية المواريث، وبيانه: أنه قال تعالى : ومِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ ﴾ النساء / ۱۱ : فرتَّب الميراث على وصية منكرة، والوصية الأولى كانت معهودةً، فلو كانت تلك الوصية باقية مع الميراث، ثم نُسخت بالسنَّة : لوجب ترتيبه على المعهودة، فصار الإطلاق نسخاً للقيد، كما يكون القيد نسخاً للإطلاق.
والثاني : أن النسخ نوعان:
أحدهما: ابتداء بعد انتهاء محض.
كتفي، فسمعته يقول: «إن الله قد أعطى كل ذي حق حقه، فلا وصية لوارث». رواه الخمسة إلا أبا داود وصححه الترمذي ورواه الخمسة إلا النسائي من حديث أبي أمامة وللدارقطني من حديث ابن عباس نحوه.
قال الشارح: وهذا الحديث في قوة المتواتر.
قلت : فلنورد ما تيسر لنا فيه فمن ذلك حديث عمرو، وحديث أبي أمامة الباهلي، وحديث ابن عباس المتقدمة وحديث ابن عمرو أخرجه الدارقطني وابن عدي من حديث حبيب المعلم عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده، وسنده حسن، وحديث أنس أخرجه ابن ماجه، وسنده حسن، وحديث علي رضي الله عنه أخرجه ابن عدي في الكامل، بسند فيه ضعف.
وأخرجه ابن أبي شيبة موقوفاً، وهو أقوى، وحديث معقل بن يسار أخرجه ابن عدي وسنده واه وحديث خارجة بن عمرو أخرجه الطبراني، وجوز أبو موسى في الذيل» أن يكون هذا هو عمرو بن خارجة.
ومن ذلك : مرسل مجاهد، أخرجه البيهقي من طريق الشافعي، ومرسل عطاء وعمرو بن دينار وأبي جعفر الباقر ، أخرها الدارقطني، والله أعلم.
والثاني بطريق الحوالة، كما نُسخت القبلة بطريق الحوالة إلى الكعبة، وهذا النسخ من القبيل الثاني.
وبيانُه : أن الله تعالى فوَّض الإيصاء في الأقربين إلى العباد بقوله تعالى: الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالأَقْرَبِينَ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ ) البقرة/ ۱۸۰ ، ثم تولى بنفسه بيان ذلك الحق، وقَصَرَه على حدود لازمة تَغيَّر بها ذلك الحق بعينه، فتحول من جهة الإيصاء إلى الميراث.
وإلى هذا أشار بقوله تعالى: ﴿ يُوصِيكُمُ اللهُ فِي أَوْلَدِ كُمْ ﴾ النساء / ١١ :
أي الذي فوض إليكم : تولى بنفسه إذ عجزتم عن مقاديره.
ألا يُرى إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تَدْرُونَ أَيُّهُمْ أَقْرَبُ لَكُمْ نَفْعًا فَرِيضَةً مِّن الله له النساء / ١١.
وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن الله تعالى أعطى كل ذي حق حقه، فلا وصية لوارث : أي بهذا الفرض نُسخ الحكم الأول وانتهى. ففي الحاصل ) لم يكن نسخاً محضاً، بل نَسْخُ تحويل من الوصية إلى الميراث، كما حولت القبلة إلى الكعبة.
(1)
ومنهم من احتج بأن قول الله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ فِي الْبُيُوتِ ﴾ النساء / ١٥: نُسخ بإثبات الرَّجم بالسنة () ، إلا أنا قد روينا عن عمر رضي
This inference is incorrect for two reasons: First: The naskh is established by the verse of inheritance. Explanation: Allah said 'after a bequest which they bequeath or a debt' (Nisa 11), thus linking inheritance to an indefinite bequest, while the first bequest was definite. If that definite bequest remained with inheritance and then was abrogated by Sunnah, it would necessitate linking it to the definite, and thus the absolute becomes an abrogation of the restricted, just as the restricted abrogates the absolute. Second: Naskh is of two types: one is absolute abrogation after complete cessation. ... I heard him say: 'Indeed Allah has given every rightful due to its owner, so no bequest to an heir.' Reported by the five except Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi authenticated it, and reported by the five except al-Nasa'i from Abu Umamah, and al-Daraqutni from Ibn Abbas similarly. The commentator said: This hadith is in the strength of mutawatir. I said: Let us mention what we can: from that is the hadith of Amr, the hadith of Abu Umamah al-Bahili, the hadith of Ibn Abbas mentioned previously, and the hadith of Ibn Amr narrated by al-Daraqutni and Ibn Adi from Habib al-Mu'allim from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather, its chain is hasan; the hadith of Anas narrated by Ibn Majah, its chain is hasan; the hadith of Ali (RA) narrated by Ibn Adi in al-Kamil with a weak chain; and Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it as mauquf, which is stronger; the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Yasar narrated by Ibn Adi with a weak chain; the hadith of Kharijah ibn Amr narrated by al-Tabarani, and Abu Musa in al-Dhayl thought this might be Amr ibn Kharijah. From that is the mursal of Mujahid narrated by al-Bayhaqi via al-Shafi'i; and the mursal of Ata, Amr ibn Dinar, and Abu Ja'far al-Baqir, narrated by al-Daraqutni. And Allah knows best. The second type is by way of conversion, just as the qibla was abrogated by conversion to the Kaaba. This naskh is of the second type. Its explanation: Allah delegated bequest for relatives to the servants saying 'Bequest for parents and relatives with kindness' (Baqara 180), then He Himself undertook the explanation of that right, and restricted it to necessary limits, thus that very right changed, converting from bequest to inheritance. And this is indicated by His saying 'Allah instructs you concerning your children' (Nisa 11): that which He delegated to you, He took upon Himself because you were incapable of its measures. Do you not see His saying 'You know not which of them is nearer to you in benefit, an ordinance from Allah' (Nisa 11). The Prophet said: 'Indeed Allah has given every rightful due to its owner, so no bequest to an heir': meaning by this apportionment the first ruling was abrogated and ended. So in the end it was not an absolute abrogation, but a naskh of conversion from bequest to inheritance, just as the qibla was converted to the Kaaba. (1) And among them is one who argued that Allah's saying 'So confine them in their homes' (Nisa 15) was abrogated by establishing stoning by the Sunnah, except that we have narrated from Umar (RA)...
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the nature of naskh (abrogation) regarding the bequest for heirs. The author responds to an opponent's argument by giving two reasons. The first reason: The naskh of the general bequest for heirs is proven by the inheritance verse (Nisa 11). The verse mentions inheritance 'after a bequest', using an indefinite term (وصية منكرة) which indicates that the previously definite bequest (وصية معهودة) was abrogated. If the earlier definite bequest had remained alongside inheritance, the verse would have linked inheritance to that definite bequest. Because it used an indefinite term, it shows the definite bequest is no longer effective. Thus the absolute (مطلق) abrogated the restricted (مقيد). The second reason: Naskh is of two types: (1) absolute abrogation (ابتداء بعد انتهاء محض) where a ruling is completely annulled and replaced, and (2) abrogation by conversion (بطريق الحوالة) where a ruling is transformed into another form, like the change of qibla. The naskh of the bequest for heirs is of the second type: Allah initially gave the right to make bequests to the people, then He Himself took over and fixed the shares of inheritance, thereby converting the obligation of bequest into fixed inheritance shares. This is indicated by the verse 'Allah instructs you concerning your children' (Nisa 11), meaning that what were previously delegated to humans, Allah now took over because they were incapable of determining the proper shares. The Prophet's hadith 'لا وصية لوارث' confirms that after the revelation of inheritance verses, the earlier ruling of bequest for heirs is abrogated. The author then lists multiple hadiths to support the mutawatir strength of this hadith. Finally, a new objection is introduced: some argue that the verse 'So confine them in their homes' (Nisa 15) was abrogated by the stoning penalty established by Sunnah. This is another example of naskh, likely brought up as a parallel argument.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revealed ruling; the text distinguishes two types: absolute (محض) and by conversion (بالحوالة).
تحويل (tahwil): A type of naskh where a ruling is not completely annulled but transformed into a different form; analogy with change of qibla.
وصية منكرة (wasiyyah munkarah): An indefinite bequest mentioned in the inheritance verse, indicating a new ruling without reference to the previous definite bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two types of naskh?
A) Absolute and conditional
B) Initial and final
C) Absolute and by conversion
D) Textual and rational

Key Takeaway
Naskh can be a conversion (tahwil) that transforms a ruling rather than simply cancelling it, as demonstrated by the shift from bequest to inheritance.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
10 min
Transformative Abrogation: From Bequest to Inheritance
Defines and exemplifies naskh al-tahwil using inheritance example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain transformative abrogation (naskh al-tahwil) as distinct from pure abrogation, and apply the analysis to given cases.

Core Idea
Abrogation can transform a ruling's modality without canceling its essence, as bequests gave way to fixed inheritance shares.

In Hanafi usul, not all abrogation (naskh) is a simple cancellation. Some rulings are transformed—their essential right is preserved but the manner of fulfillment changes. The classic example is the shift from voluntary bequests to obligatory inheritance shares. Al-Bazdawi explains this 'transformative abrogation' (naskh al-tahwil) using the Qur'anic verses on bequests and inheritance, showing that Allah Himself took over the right He had previously delegated. This lesson walks through that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary texts
Locate the verse on bequests (al-Baqara 2:180) and the verse on inheritance (an-Nisa 4:11). Note how the first gives a general permission, while the second imposes fixed shares.
Also note the hadith: 'no bequest for an heir' as a confirming evidence.
2
Determine the type of inter-textual relationship
Analyze whether the second text cancels the first completely (naskh mahd) or changes its modality (naskh al-tahwil). The author argues for tahwil because the same right (relatives' share) persists but is now mandated by Allah rather than left to human discretion.
The analogy with the qibla change illustrates that the essence (facing a direction) remains, while the specific direction changed.
3
Examine the mechanism of transformation (hawālah)
Identify how the ruling changed: from tafwīḍ (delegation) to ta‘yīn (determination). Allah says He undertook (tawallā) the clarification Himself because humans were incapable of measuring shares.
The key phrase: 'ghayyara bihā dhālika al-ḥaqq bi-‘aynihi' – that very right changed.
4
Contrast with pure abrogation
Understand that in naskh mahd the earlier ruling is completely replaced with no continuity of essence. Here the right is not abolished but transformed. The hadith 'lā waṣiyyata li-wārith' confirms the end of the first ruling, but the obligation to provide for relatives continues via inheritance.
This distinction is important for usul reasoning: a ruling may be overridden in form but not in spirit.
5
Apply the concept to other cases
Consider other potential examples of naskh al-tahwil, such as the change of qibla or the gradual prohibition of wine. Identify whether the essence of the act remains.
Not all changes are tahwil; many are pure naskh or specification (takhṣīṣ).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني بطريق الحوالة، كما نُسخت القبلة بطريق الحوالة إلى الكعبة، وهذا النسخ من القبيل الثاني. وبيانُه : أن الله تعالى فوَّض الإيصاء في الأقربين إلى العباد بقوله تعالى: الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالأَقْرَبِينَ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ ) البقرة/ ۱۸۰ ، ثم تولى بنفسه بيان ذلك الحق، وقَصَرَه على حدود لازمة تَغيَّر بها ذلك الحق بعينه، فتحول من جهة الإيصاء إلى الميراث. وإلى هذا أشار بقوله تعالى: ﴿ يُوصِيكُمُ اللهُ فِي أَوْلَدِ كُمْ ﴾ النساء / ١١ : أي الذي فوض إليكم : تولى بنفسه إذ عجزتم عن مقاديره. ألا يُرى إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تَدْرُونَ أَيُّهُمْ أَقْرَبُ لَكُمْ نَفْعًا فَرِيضَةً مِّن الله له النساء / ١١. وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن الله تعالى أعطى كل ذي حق حقه، فلا وصية لوارث : أي بهذا الفرض نُسخ الحكم الأول وانتهى. ففي الحاصل ) لم يكن نسخاً محضاً، بل نَسْخُ تحويل من الوصية إلى الميراث، كما حولت القبلة إلى الكعبة. (1) جملة ونفي الحاصل... إلى قوله إلى الكعبة مثبتة في نسخة ٨٦٨هـ و ٨١٥ هـ ، دون غيرهما. سائد.
And the second type is by way of transformation, just as the qibla was abrogated by way of transformation to the Kaaba, and this abrogation is of the second type. And its explanation: that Allah the Exalted delegated the bequest to relatives to the servants by His statement: 'The bequest is for parents and the nearest by the known' (al-Baqara 2:180), then He Himself undertook to clarify that right, and limited it to obligatory shares, by which that very right changed, so it transformed from the aspect of bequest to inheritance. And to this He referred by His statement: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children' (an-Nisa 4:11) meaning that which He delegated to you: He undertook it Himself when you were incapable of its measures. Do you not see His statement: 'You do not know which of them is nearer to you in benefit, an obligation from Allah' (an-Nisa 4:11). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed Allah the Exalted has given every right-holder his right, so no bequest for an heir,' meaning by this obligation the first ruling was abrogated and ended. So in reality, it was not pure abrogation, but abrogation of transformation from bequest to inheritance, just as the qibla was transformed to the Kaaba. (1) The sentence 'and the negation of al-haasil... up to his saying to the Kaaba' is confirmed in the copies of 868 AH and 815 AH, not in others. Sa'id.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage defines and exemplifies transformative abrogation (naskh al-tahwil), a key concept in Hanafi usul. The commentator contrasts it with pure abrogation (naskh mahd). The example: the pre-Islamic practice of voluntary bequests to relatives was initially confirmed by the Qur'an (al-Baqara 2:180) as a delegation to individuals. Later, Allah Himself fixed the shares of inheritance (an-Nisa 4:11), transforming the same right from a discretionary bequest into a mandatory distribution. This is not a complete cancellation but a change in modality. The commentator cites the hadith 'no bequest for an heir' to show that the earlier ruling is superseded. The footnote clarifies that this explanation is found in specific manuscripts. The analogy with the change of qibla reinforces that the essence of worship (facing a direction) remains, while the specific direction changed.

Key Terms
نسخ تحويل (naskh al-tahwīl): Abrogation that changes the modality of a ruling while its essential content remains
حوالة (ḥawālah): Transformation, especially as a type of naskh that shifts a ruling's application
تولي (tawallī): Undertaking personally; used to describe Allah taking charge of a previously delegated right
تفويض (tafwīḍ): Delegation; the initial state where humans were entrusted to determine bequests

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of abrogation is demonstrated by the replacement of bequests for relatives with fixed inheritance shares?
A) Pure abrogation (naskh mahd)
B) Transformative abrogation (naskh al-tahwil)
C) Gradual abrogation (naskh tadrījī)
D) Specification (takhṣīṣ)

Key Takeaway
Transformative abrogation preserves the essence of a right while changing its modality, as seen in the shift from bequest to inheritance.

Naskh — Abrogation

Refuting Claims of Quran Abrogated by Sunnah
Refutes claims that Quranic verses are abrogated by sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position against naskh al-Qur'an bi al-sunnah and evaluate the evidence for treating the stoning verse as originally Quranic.

Core Idea
A sunnah cannot abrogate a Quranic ruling; alleged cases involve either original Quranic status or contextual interpretation.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul confronts a delicate usul question: Can a sunnah (hadith) abrogate a Quranic verse? Some scholars argue that certain verses were superseded by prophetic practice. The commentator, following the Hanafi school, refutes these claims by reanalyzing the textual history and context. The refutation turns on two key moves: citing Umar's testimony that the stoning verse was once part of the Quran, and interpreting the Mumtahina verse as a specific financial assistance ruling, not a general law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed instances of naskh
Locate the two verses that opponents allege are abrogated by the sunnah: the confinement verse (4:15) and the compensation verse (60:11).
These appear in the first and second arguments of the passage.
2
Examine the Hanafi refutation for each claim
For the first claim, note the citation of Umar's testimony that stoning was recited in the Quran. For the second, note the contextual interpretation involving apostasy and spoils.
The commentator rejects both as 'ghayr sahih' (not correct).
3
Locate the key evidences
Identify Umar's statement (muttafaq 'alayh) as evidence that the stoning verse was originally Quranic. Identify the contextual reading of al-Mumtahina 11 as assistance from spoils.
These are the dala'il for the Hanafi position.
4
Distinguish between abrogation and specification
Understand that the commentator treats these cases as takhsis (specification) or bayan (clarification), not naskh. The stoning hadith does not abrogate a current verse but implements a former one.
This preserves the principle that Quran is not abrogated by sunnah.
5
Apply the principle to similar claims
When encountering an apparent contradiction between a verse and a hadith, first check if the hadith can be interpreted as a specification or if the verse's history reveals prior abrogation of recitation.
This methodological step prevents incorrect claims of naskh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من احتج بأن قول الله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ فِي الْبُيُوتِ ﴾ النساء / ١٥: نُسخ بإثبات الرَّجم بالسنة () ، إلا أنا قد روينا عن عمر رضي الله عنه : أن الرجم كان مما يُتلى في كتاب الله » . ولأن قوله جل وعلا: أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلًا اله النساء / ١٥: ﴾ مجمل (√) فسرته السنة (٢) واحتج بعضهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن فَاتَكُمْ شَيْءٌ مِّنْ أَزْوَاجِكُمْ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ ) الآية، الممتحنة / ۱۱ : فإن هذا حكم نُسخ بالسنة (۳) . وهذا غير صحيح؛ لأن هذا كان فيمن ارتدَّت امرأته، ولحقت بدار الحرب أن يُعطى ما غرم فيها زوجها المسلم؛ معونةً له. وفي ذلك أقوال مختلفة، وقد قيل : إنه غير منسوخ إن كان المراد به الإعانة من الغنيمة، فيكون معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿فَعَاقَبتُم الممتحنة / ١١ : أي غنمتم. (۱) قوله : عن عمر أن الرجم كان مما يُتلى : عن ابن عباس سمعت عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه يخطب ويقول : إن الله بعث محمداً بالحق، وأنزل عليه الكتاب، فكان مما أنزل عليه آية الرجم، فقرأناها ووعيناها، ورَجَمَ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورجمنا بعده، وأخشى إن طال بالناس زمن أن يقول قائل : ما نجد الرجم في كتاب الله، فيضلوا بترك فريضة أنزلها الله في كتابه، حقٌّ على من زنا إذا أحصن من الرجال والنساء إذا قامت البينةُ، أو كان حمل، أو اعتراف». الحديث. متفق عليه. (۲) قوله : مجمل فرتْه السنة : يعني حديث: خذوا عني، خذوا عني، قد جعل الله لهن سبيلاً»، وقد تقدم في باب الطعن يلحق الحديث من قبل راويه [ص٤٤١]. (۳) قوله : نُسخ بالسنة : يعني إيتاء الزوج مثل ما أنفق، قال الشارح: أي لا يُتلى ناسخه في القرآن، ولم يذكر خبراً ولا أثراً.
And among them is one who argued with the statement of Allah the Exalted: 'So keep them in the houses' (an-Nisa 4:15) is abrogated by establishing stoning through the sunnah, except that we have narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that stoning was among what was recited in the Book of Allah. And because His statement, Glorified and Exalted: 'Or Allah makes for them a way' (an-Nisa 4:15) is ambiguous (mujmal) interpreted by the sunnah. And some argued with His statement: 'And if anything of your wives slips away from you to the disbelievers' (al-Mumtahina 11) — this ruling is abrogated by the sunnah. And this is not correct; because this was in the case of a woman who apostatized and joined the abode of war, that her Muslim husband should be given what he spent on her, as assistance for him. And there are differing opinions about that, and it has been said that it is not abrogated if what is meant is assistance from the spoils, so the meaning of His statement: 'and you have retaliated' (al-Mumtahina 11) is: you gained spoils. (1) His statement: from Umar that stoning was among what was recited: from Ibn Abbas: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab giving a sermon and saying: 'Indeed Allah sent Muhammad with truth and revealed the Book to him, and among what was revealed was the verse of stoning; we recited it and memorized it, and the Messenger of Allah stoned and we stoned after him...' the hadith, agreed upon. (2) His statement: mujmal interpreted by the sunnah: meaning the hadith 'Take from me, take from me, Allah has made a way for them', and it has preceded in the chapter on accusation attached to the hadith from its transmitter [p.441]. (3) His statement: abrogated by the sunnah: meaning giving the husband the equivalent of what he spent; the commentator said: i.e., its abrogator is not recited in the Quran, and he did not mention any report or effect.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage engages in a usul dispute about whether the Quran can be abrogated by the sunnah. The commentator presents two claims made by some scholars: (1) that the verse commanding confinement of adulteresses (an-Nisa 4:15) is abrogated by the hadith of stoning, and (2) that the verse about compensation for a lost wife (al-Mumtahina 11) is abrogated by sunnah. The commentator refutes both. For the first, he cites Umar's testimony that the stoning verse was originally part of the Quranic text—implying it was abrogation of recitation, not abrogation of a Quranic ruling by sunnah. For the second, he explains the context: it addresses a specific situation (apostate wife) and the compensation is from spoils, not a new ruling. The footnote clarifies the hadith of stoning and the hadith 'take from me, take from me' which explains the 'way' in the verse. The commentator concludes that these are not instances of abrogation by sunnah, but rather specification (takhsis) or clarification (bayan).

Key Terms
مجمل (mujmal): A text that is ambiguous and requires external clarification (by sunnah)
نسخ بالسنة (naskh bi al-sunnah): Claimed abrogation of a Quranic ruling by a hadith; rejected here

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator refute the claim that the verse 'keep them in the houses' (an-Nisa 4:15) is abrogated by the stoning hadith?
A) Because the hadith is considered weak in transmission
B) Because the stoning verse was originally part of the Quranic text
C) Because the verse is not applicable to married adulterers
D) Because the sunnah cannot abrogate the Quran under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
Not every difference between a verse and a hadith is abrogation; one must consider textual history, context, and the principle that sunnah does not abrogate Quran.

Refutation of Claim of Abrogation of al-Mumtahinah Verse by Sunnah
Refutes a claim that a Quranic verse was abrogated by the Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a claim of naskh by contextualizing the ruling and applying the Hanafi principle that context determines applicability.

Core Idea
A ruling specific to a unique situation is not subject to general abrogation.

Claims of naskh must be scrutinized carefully. In this passage, the author refutes an assertion that a Quranic verse was abrogated by the Sunnah, showing that the verse's context—apostate wives and spoils of war—keeps it operative. Understanding the proper conditions for naskh is essential for sound istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its basis
Some scholars claim that Surah al-Mumtahinah 60:11 was abrogated by an unspecified Sunnah. Identify which verse and which alleged abrogator are involved.
The opposing argument is presented but not attributed to a specific school.
2
Examine the verse's context
Analyze the situation described: a Muslim husband loses his wife to apostasy and war. The ruling provides compensation from spoils. This specificity is key.
The verse does not address general divorce or loss.
3
Apply Hanafi conditions for naskh
For naskh, three conditions must be met: (1) the abrogating text must be later, (2) the earlier ruling must be general or unconditional, and (3) there must be clear evidence of abrogation. Here, the ruling is conditional and specific, so it cannot be abrogated by a general Sunnah.
Hanafis permit naskh of Quran by Sunnah if the Sunnah is mutawatir or known, but context precludes it.
4
Conclude the ruling remains operative
The author concludes that the verse is not abrogated because it was only for a specific situation. The interpretation of 'fa'āqabtum' as 'you gained spoils' supports this reading.
This preserves the ruling for its original context, which remains applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن قوله جل وعلا: ﴿أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللهُ لَهُنَّ سَبِيلًا﴾ [النساء / ١٥] مجمل (√) فسرته السنة (٢) واحتج بعضهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن فَاتَكُمْ شَيْءٌ مِّنْ أَزْوَاجِكُمْ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ﴾ الآية، الممتحنة / ۱۱ : فإن هذا حكم نُسخ بالسنة (۳) . وهذا غير صحيح؛ لأن هذا كان فيمن ارتدَّت امرأته، ولحقت بدار الحرب أن يُعطى ما غرم فيها زوجها المسلم؛ معونةً له. وفي ذلك أقوال مختلفة، وقد قيل : إنه غير منسوخ إن كان المراد به الإعانة من الغنيمة، فيكون معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿فَعَاقَبتُم﴾ الممتحنة / ١١ : أي غنمتم.
And because His saying, Exalted is He: 'Or God make for them a way' [Quran 4:15] is ambiguous, the Sunnah explained it. And some people argued using His saying: 'And if you lose anything of your wives to the disbelievers' [Quran 60:11] that this ruling was abrogated by the Sunnah. But this is incorrect because this was regarding a woman who apostatized and joined the land of war, that her Muslim husband should be given what he spent as support for him. There are different opinions about it, and it has been said that it is not abrogated if the intended meaning is the assistance from the spoils, so the meaning of His saying: 'And you have exacted your due' [60:11] is 'you have gained spoils.'
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage refutes a claim that a Quranic verse was abrogated by the Sunnah. The text first notes that the verse in Surah al-Nisa' is mujmal (ambiguous) and requires explanation, which the Sunnah provided. Then it addresses the claim that the verse in Surah al-Mumtahinah (60:11) was abrogated by the Sunnah. The author rejects this by contextualizing the verse: it concerns a specific situation where a Muslim husband lost his wife to apostasy and war, entitling him to compensation. Thus, the ruling is not abrogated but rather remains in effect for its specific context. The author mentions that some hold it is not abrogated if the assistance is from spoils, interpreting 'fa'āqabtum' as 'you gained spoils'. This shows that for naskh to be claimed, one must ensure the ruling's context is properly understood.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.
مجمل (mujmal): A text that is ambiguous and requires explanation (bayan) from another source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the verse is ambiguous and the Sunnah explains it

Key Takeaway
A ruling revealed for a specific context is not automatically abrogated by a later general Sunnah; context determines naskh applicability.

The Qibla Example: Proving Mutual Naskh Between Quran and Sunnah
Provides historical evidence that Quran and Sunnah mutually abrogate each other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi evidence for mutual naskh between the Quran and Sunnah using the qibla change example and apply the istinbat chain to derive the ruling of permissibility.

Core Idea
The qibla changed from Quran to Sunnah and back, proving that each can abrogate the other.

This lesson examines a key historical proof cited by Imam al-Pazdawi in Kanz al-Wusul. The qibla change demonstrates that both the Quran and the Sunnah have abrogatory authority over each other. Understanding this evidence is essential for the Hanafi position on the scope of naskh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the qibla sequence
The first ruling (facing Kaaba) was from the Quran; the second (facing Bayt al-Maqdis) from the Sunnah; the third (return to Kaaba) from the Quran again.
This sequence is the core historical evidence.
2
Classify each abrogation event
First abrogation: Quran by Sunnah. Second abrogation: Sunnah by Quran. This shows mutual naskh.
3
Extract the istinbat chain
Trace the three-step derivation from the text: observation of initial ruling, naskh by Sunnah, then naskh by Quran.
Refer to the istinbat_chain block below.
4
Note the broader implication
The passage also notes that previous scriptures were abrogated by Islamic sharia, further supporting the principle of naskh across different revelation sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الحجة الدالة على أنه يجوز نسخ الكتاب بالسنة، ونسخ السنة بالكتاب : أن التوجه إلى الكعبة في الابتداء إن ثبت بالكتاب: فقد نُسخ بالسنة الموجبة للتوجه إلى بيت المقدس والثابت بالسنة من التوجه إلى بيت المقدس: نُسخ بالكتاب. والشرائع الثابتة بالكتب السالفة : نُسخت بشريعتنا، وما ثبت ذلك إلا بني (٦)
And among the evidence indicating that it is permissible to abrogate the Book by the Sunnah and the Sunnah by the Book: that the initial facing of the Kaaba, if established by the Book, was abrogated by the Sunnah which required facing Bayt al-Maqdis, and the facing of Bayt al-Maqdis established by the Sunnah was abrogated by the Book. And the laws established by previous scriptures were abrogated by our sharia, and that is only established by binī (?)
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage presents a key proof for the permissibility of mutual abrogation between the Quran and the Sunnah. The author uses the historical example of the qibla change: initially, Muslims faced the Kaaba (established by the Quran), then they were commanded by the Sunnah to face Bayt al-Maqdis (abrogating the Quranic ruling), and later the Quran abrogated the Sunnah by commanding the Kaaba again. This demonstrates that abrogation occurs in both directions. Additionally, the author notes that previous divine laws were abrogated by the Islamic sharia, which is a broader point about naskh across different revelations.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): The lifting of a ruling by a later evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The abrogation of the stoning verse
C) The abrogation of the verse about giving compensation
D) The abrogation of previous scriptures

Key Takeaway
The qibla change demonstrates that the Quran and Sunnah can mutually abrogate each other.

Proof of Cross-Abrogation Between Qur'an and Sunnah
Proofs for cross-abrogation between Qur'an and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on cross-abrogation and identify at least three historical examples from the source.

Core Idea
Cross-abrogation between Qur'an and Sunnah is proven by multiple instances including the qibla change and treaty of Hudaybiyyah.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi proof that the Qur'an can be abrogated by the Sunnah and vice versa. The text cites several historical events to demonstrate that this has occurred, reinforcing the principle that later revelation can supersede earlier rulings regardless of type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The passage aims to prove that it is permissible for the Qur'an to abrogate the Sunnah and for the Sunnah to abrogate the Qur'an. Recognise this as the central claim.
2
Examine each proof
Read each example: qibla change, Ubayy hadith, 'A'ishah's statement, treaty of Hudaybiyyah, and previous scriptures. For each, note which type of evidence abrogates which.
The qibla change shows Sunnah abrogating Qur'an (initially) and then Qur'an abrogating Sunnah; this is a double proof.
3
Evaluate the response to the opposing view
The passage implicitly counters those who restrict naskh to same-type by providing concrete examples. Understand that Hanafis allow cross-abrogation when the later evidence is mutawatir or mashhur.
The Ubayy hadith also shows that abrogation requires explicit notification, which can come via Sunnah.
4
Summarise the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that many fiqh rulings where a later Prophetic practice overrides an earlier Qur'anic verse remain valid. Without this principle, such rulings would be inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الحجة الدالة على أنه يجوز نسخ الكتاب بالسنة، ونسخ السنة بالكتاب : أن التوجه إلى الكعبة في الابتداء إن ثبت بالكتاب: فقد نُسخ بالسنة الموجبة للتوجه إلى بيت المقدس والثابت بالسنة من التوجه إلى بيت المقدس: نُسخ بالكتاب. والشرائع الثابتة بالكتب السالفة : نُسخت بشريعتنا، وما ثبت ذلك إلا بتبليغ الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام. وتَرَكَ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم آيةً في قراءته، فلما أخبر به : قال: ألم يكن فيكم أُبي! فقال : بلى يا رسول الله، لكني ظننت أنها نُسخت، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: لو نُسخت: لأخبرتكم». وإنما ظنَّ النسخ من غير كتاب يُتلى، ولم يَرُدَّ عليه. وقالت عائشة رضي الله عنها: «ما قبض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حتى أباح الله تعالى له من النساء ما شاء»، فكان نسخاً للكتاب بالسنة. وصالَحَ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أهل مكة على ردّ نسائهم، ثم نُسخ ذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ عَلِمْتُمُوهُنَّ مُؤْمِنَ فَلَا تَرْجِعُوهُنَّ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ﴾
Among the proofs that it is permissible to abrogate the Book by the Sunnah, and the Sunnah by the Book, is that the facing toward the Ka'bah initially, if established by the Book, was abrogated by the Sunnah requiring facing toward Bayt al-Maqdis; and what was established by the Sunnah of facing toward Bayt al-Maqdis was abrogated by the Book. The laws established by previous Books were abrogated by our law, and that was only established by the conveying of the Messenger, peace be upon him. And the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, left out a verse in his recitation. When he was informed, he said: 'Was not Ubayy among you?' He said: 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah, but I thought it had been abrogated.' He said: 'If it had been abrogated, I would have informed you.' And he thought it was abrogated without a recited text, and he did not reject him. And 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with her, said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, did not die until Allah Almighty permitted for him from women whatever he wished.' So that was an abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah. And the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, made a treaty with the people of Makkah regarding returning their women, then that was abrogated by His statement: 'And if you know them to be believers, do not return them to the disbelievers.'
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage presents multiple proofs that the Qur'an can be abrogated by the Sunnah and the Sunnah by the Qur'an, a position held by the Hanafi school. The first proof is the change of qibla: initially, prayer toward the Ka'bah was established by the Qur'an (and according to some, by practice), then abrogated by the Sunnah commanding toward Bayt al-Maqdis, and later that Sunnah was abrogated by the Qur'anic verse commanding toward the Ka'bah again. This shows cross-abrogation. The second proof: previous divine laws were abrogated by our Shari'ah, and that abrogation was only conveyed through the Prophet's message (Sunnah), so the Sunnah abrogates previous revelations. The third proof: the incident where the Prophet left out a verse in recitation and Ubayy thought it was abrogated, but the Prophet denied abrogation, implying that if it had been abrogated, he would have informed them. This shows that abrogation requires notification, and that notification can come through the Prophet's words or actions, which are Sunnah. The fourth proof: 'A'ishah's statement that Allah permitted the Prophet extra wives near his death, which abrogated the earlier Qur'anic limit of four wives—this is abrogation of Qur'an by Sunnah (since the permission is recorded in hadith, not in the Qur'an). The fifth proof: the treaty of Hudaybiyyah included returning women believers to Quraysh, but this was abrogated by the Qur'anic verse prohibiting their return (Quran 60:10). This shows abrogation of a Sunnah ruling (the treaty term) by the Qur'an. Collectively, these examples demonstrate that cross-abrogation is valid and occurred historically.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: the removal of a Shari'ah ruling by a later evidence, as applied to cross-text types.
الكتاب (al-kitab): The Qur'an, the revealed book of Allah.
السنة (al-sunnah): The words, actions, and approvals of the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which historical event is used in this passage as an example of the Sunnah abrogating a Qur'anic ruling?
A) The change of qibla from the Ka'bah to Bayt al-Maqdis.
B) The treaty of Hudaybiyyah regarding returning women.
C) The permission for extra wives after the limit of four.
D) The incident of Ubayy and the verse recitation.

Key Takeaway
Cross-abrogation between Qur'an and Sunnah is established by multiple historical examples, supporting the Hanafi position that later revelation of any type can supersede earlier rulings, provided the abrogating evidence is sufficiently reliable.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
8 min
Abrogation of the Quran by Sunnah: Evidence from the Prophet's Practice
Proves that Sunnah can abrogate Quran using two historical examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state two historical proofs used by the Hanafis to establish that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Sunnah can abrogate the Quran, as proven by the Prophet's informed practice and the Quranic abrogation of the Hudaybiyyah treaty.

One of the most debated issues in usul al-fiqh is whether the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran. The Hanafi school holds that it can, based on clear evidence from the Prophet's own practice and subsequent Quranic revelation. In this lesson, we examine two key proofs: the incident of Ubayy ibn Ka'b and the treaty of Hudaybiyyah concerning the return of women. These examples demonstrate that abrogation is not confined to Quran abrogating Quran; rather, the Sunnah, as a source of revelation, can also effect naskh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
The passage presents two distinct proofs: (1) the Prophet's statement to Ubayy ibn Ka'b regarding a verse he thought was abrogated, and (2) the change in ruling on returning emigrant women, where a Sunnah-based treaty was later abrogated by a Quranic verse. Recognize that both are intended to show the Sunnah's capacity to abrogate the Quran.
2
Analyze the first proof (Ubayy incident)
When the Prophet omitted a verse in recitation, Ubayy assumed it was abrogated. The Prophet responded, 'If it were abrogated, I would have informed you.' This implies that abrogation is announced through revelation (which includes Sunnah). The Prophet's statement itself is a Sunnah proof that abrogation can occur through his communication.
The Prophet's word 'أخبرتكم' (I would have informed you) indicates that abrogation requires informing, and his informing is part of the Sunnah.
3
Analyze the second proof (Hudaybiyyah treaty and Aisha's report)
The treaty of Hudaybiyyah included a condition that Muslim women emigrating to Medina must be returned. This was a Sunnah-based agreement. Later, the Quranic verse from Surat al-Mumtahanah (60:10) prohibited returning believing women. This abrogated the earlier Sunnah rule. Additionally, Aisha reported that the Prophet's permission to marry many women abrogated earlier limits, showing Sunnah abrogating Quran.
The second proof is two-fold: the Quran abrogating Sunnah (the treaty) and Sunnah abrogating Quran (Aisha's narration). Both support the bidirectional possibility.
4
Connect the proofs to the ruling
The Hanafi position that Sunnah can abrogate Quran is based on these events, which show actual occurrence of such abrogation. The Shafi'i school denies this, arguing that only Quran can abrogate Quran. However, the Hanafis argue that the Sunnah is also divinely revealed, so it carries equal authority for abrogation.
The key is that the Sunnah is a form of revelation (wahy), thus it can lift a Quranic ruling, just as Quran can lift a Sunnah ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بتبليغ الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام. وتَرَكَ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم آيةً في قراءته، فلما أخبر به قال: ألم يكن فيكم أُبي! فقال: بلى يا رسول الله، لكني ظننت أنها نُسخت، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: لو نُسخت لأخبرتكم. وإنما ظنَّ النسخ من غير كتاب يُتلى، ولم يَرُدَّ عليه. وقالت عائشة رضي الله عنها: «ما قبض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حتى أباح الله تعالى له من النساء ما شاء»، فكان نسخاً للكتاب بالسنة. وصالَحَ رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أهل مكة على ردّ نسائهم، ثم نُسخ ذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ عَلِمْتُمُوهُنَّ مُؤْمِنَاتٍ فَلَا تَرْجِعُوهُنَّ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ﴾ [الممتحنة: 10]. وعند البخاري: فجاء نسوة مؤمنات، فأنزل الله: {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا} حتى بلغ {الْكَوَافِرَ}. عن مروان والمسور قالا: لما كاتب سهيل بن عمرو يومئذ كان فيما اشترط سهيل على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه لا يأتيك منا أحد وإن كان على دينك إلا رددته إلينا، وخليت بيننا وبينه فكره المؤمنون ذلك، وامتعضوا منه، وأبي سهيل إلا ذلك، فكاتبه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فردَّ يومئذ أبا جندل إلى أبيه سهيل، ولم يأته أحد من الرجال إلا ردَّه في تلك المدة وإن كان مسلماً. وجاءت المؤمنات مهاجرات، وكانت أم كلثوم بنت عقبة بن أبي معيط ممن خرج إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يومئذ وهي عاتق، فجاء أهلها يسألون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يرجعها إليهم، فلم يرجعها إليهم؛ لِمَا أنزل الله فيهن: {إِذَا جَاءَكُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتُ مُهَاجِرَاتٍ فَامْتَحِنُوهُنَّ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِإِيمَانِهِنَّ} إلى {وَلَا هُمْ يَحِلُّونَ لَهُنَّ}. رواه البخاري. وله عن الزهري قال عروة: فأخبرتني عائشة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يمتحنهن.
By conveying the message of the Messenger, peace be upon him. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, left out a verse in his recitation. When he was informed, he said: 'Is there not among you Ubayy?' He said: 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah, but I thought it was abrogated.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'If it were abrogated, I would have informed you.' And he thought abrogation from a book not recited, and he did not reject it. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not die until Allah permitted him of women what He willed.' So that was an abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, made a peace treaty with the people of Mecca on the condition of returning their women, then that was abrogated by His statement: 'And if you know them to be believers, do not return them to the disbelievers' [Quran 60:10]. And according to Bukhari: Then believing women came, and Allah revealed: 'O you who believe, do not...' until 'the disbelieving women.' From Marwan and al-Miswar: They said: When Suhayl ibn Amr made the treaty that day, among the conditions Suhayl imposed on the Prophet, peace be upon him, was that if anyone from us comes to you, even if he is on your religion, you must return him to us and leave us alone with him. The believers disliked that and were distressed, but Suhayl insisted on it. So the Prophet, peace be upon him, made the treaty with him and returned Abu Jandal to his father Suhayl that day, and no man came to him except he returned him during that period even if he was Muslim. And believing women came as emigrants, among them Umm Kulthum bint Uqba ibn Abi Mu'ayt, who went out to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that day while she was unmarried. Her family came asking the Prophet, peace be upon him, to return her to them, but he did not return her because of what Allah revealed concerning them: 'When believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them; Allah knows best their faith...' until 'nor are they lawful for them.' Narrated by Bukhari. And from him from al-Zuhri, Urwa said: Aisha told me that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, used to examine them.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a usul argument proving that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran, against those who hold that only the Quran can abrogate the Quran. The author, al-Bazdawi, presents two proofs. First: the incident where the Prophet forgot a verse and Ubayy ibn Ka'b thought it was abrogated. The Prophet replied that if it were abrogated, he would have informed them, implying that abrogation occurs through revelation, and the Prophet's statement indicates that Sunnah can effect naskh. Second: the treaty of Hudaybiyyah included a condition that Muslim women emigrating to Medina must be returned. This condition was later abrogated by the Quranic verse from Surat al-Mumtahanah (60:10) which prohibited returning believing women. Here, a Sunnah action (the treaty) was abrogated by a Quranic verse, showing that abrogation can go either way. The author also cites Aisha's hadith that Allah permitted the Prophet many women, which abrogated the earlier limitation; this was a Sunnah-based permission abrogating a Quranic rule. The passage concludes with a detailed narration from Bukhari about the examination of emigrant women, confirming that the Prophet followed the new revelation. Thus, the text establishes that naskh of the Quran by the Sunnah is permissible and occurred historically.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): The lifting (رفع) of a previously established legal ruling by a later revealed evidence (dalil) from the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of Sunnah abrogating Quran?
A) The Prophet's recitation leaving out a verse
B) Aisha's statement that Allah permitted the Prophet many women
C) The treaty of Hudaybiyyah requiring return of women
D) The Quranic verse forbidding return of believing women

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah can abrogate the Quran, as proven by the Prophet's statement to Ubayy and the change in ruling on returning women after the treaty of Hudaybiyyah.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
The Rational Proof for Sunnah Abrogating the Quran's Ruling
Rational proof for cross-abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rational proof for why the Sunnah can abrogate a ruling of the Quran, and apply it to distinguish between abrogation of ruling vs wording.

Core Idea
The Sunnah is revelation; it can clarify the duration of a Quranic ruling without altering its wording.

In this lesson, we unpack the rational argument presented by the author for the permissibility of the Sunnah abrogating a ruling of the Quran. The key insight is that abrogation is merely clarification of the time limit of a ruling, and the Prophet was sent as an explainer. This positions the Sunnah as an authoritative source for abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Define abrogation as clarification of duration
Understand that naskh is not nullification but indicating the end of a ruling's applicability.
2
Identify the Prophet's role as explainer
The Prophet was sent to explain the Book; therefore, he can clarify when a ruling's duration ends.
3
Distinguish between ruling and wording
The Sunnah only abrogates the ruling, not the Quranic text itself.
This preserves the Quran's textual integrity.
4
Recognize the Sunnah's status as revelation
The verse 'Nor does he speak from desire' (53:3) affirms that the Prophet's speech is divine revelation.
Equal in ruling authority.
5
Apply the proof to counter opposition
The Hanafi response: if Sunnah couldn't abrogate Quran, abrogation within Quran and Sunnah would also be invalid.
This elevates the Prophet's station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل المعقول: أن النسخ بيان مدة الحكم، وجائز للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بيان حكم الكتاب، فقد بُعث مبيناً، وجائز أن يتولى الله تعالى بيان ما أجرى على لسان رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم. ولأن الكتاب يزيد بنظمه على السُّنَّة، فلا يُشكل أنه يَصلُح ناسخاً. وأما السُّنَّة : فإنما يُنسَخُ بها حكم الكتاب، دون نَظْمه، والسُّنَّةُ في حق الحكم وحي مطلق توجِبُ ما يوجبه الكتاب، فإذا بقي النظم الكتاب، وانتسخ الحكم منه بالسنَّة : كان المنسوخ مثل الناسخ، لا محالة. ولو وقع الطعن بمثله : لما صح ذلك في الكتاب بالكتاب والسنة بالسنَّة، بل في ذلك إعلاء منزلة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وتعظيم سنته، والله أعلم. وظهر أنه ليس بتبديل من تلقاء نفسه؛ لأنه جل وعلا قال: ﴿ وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى ﴾ [النجم: 3]. وبلغنا أنه لما أنزل الله أن يَرُدُّوا إلى المشركين ما أنفقوا على من هاجر من أزواجهم ، وحكم على المسلمين: ﴿وَلَا تُمْسِكُوا بِعِصَمِ الْكَوَافِرِ﴾ أن قريبة بنت أبي أمية، وابنة جرول الخزاعي، فتزوج قُرَيْبةَ معاوية، وتزوج الأخرى أبو جهم، فلما أبى الكفار أن يُقِرُّوا بأداء ما أنفق المسلمون على أزواجهم: أنزل الله : ﴿وَإِن فَاتَكُمْ شَيْءٌ مِّنْ أَزْوَاجِكُمْ إِلَى الْكُفَّارِ فَعَاقَبْتُمْ﴾، والعقب: ما يؤدي المسلمون إلى من هاجرت امرأته من الكفار، فأمر أن يُعطى من ذهب له زوج من المسلمين ما أنفق من صداق نساء الكفار اللاتي هاجرن، وما نعلم أن أحداً من المهاجرات ارتدت بعد إيمانها. وأما الحديث : فدليل على أن الكتاب يجوز أن يَنسخ السُّنَّةَ. وتأويل الحديث أن العرض على الكتاب: إنما يجب فيما أشكل تاريخه، أو لم يكن في الصحة، بحيث يُنسخ به الكتاب، فكان تقديم الكتاب أولى. فأما قوله جل وعلا: ﴿نَأْتِ بِخَيْرٍ مِنْهَا أَوْ مِثْلِهَا﴾ [البقرة: 106]: فإن المراد بالخيرية : فيما يرجع إلى مرافق العباد دون النظم بمعناه، فكذلك المماثلة. على أنا قد بينا أن نسخ حكم الكتاب بالسنة خارج عن هذه الجملة. ونَسْخُ السنَّة بالسنة : مثل قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إني كنتُ نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور ألا فزوروها، فقد أذن لمحمد في زيارة قبر أمه وكنت نهيتكم عن لحوم الأضاحي أن تُمسكوها فوق ثلاثة أيام: فأمسكوها ما بدا لكم، وكنتُ نهيتكم عن النبيذ في الدباء والحَنْتَم والنقير والمُرَفَّت، فاشربوا في كل ظرف فإن الظرف لا يُحِلَّ شيئاً ، ولا يُحرمه). ونَسْخُ خبر الواحد بمثله : جائز أيضاً. عن ابن بريدة عن أبيه قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور فزوروها، ونهيتكم لحوم الأضاحي فوق ثلاث فأمسكوا ما بدا لكم ونهيتكم عن النبيذ إلا في سقاء: فاشربوا في الأوعية، ولا تشربوا مسكراً. رواه مسلم. وللترمذي عنه قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «كنت نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور، فقد أذن لمحمد في زيارة قبر أمه، فزوروها؛ فإنها تُذكر الآخرة».
The rational proof: that abrogation is the clarification of the duration of a ruling, and it is permissible for the Messenger, peace be upon him, to clarify the ruling of the Book, for he was sent as an explainer, and it is permissible for Allah Almighty to undertake the clarification of what is uttered upon the tongue of His Messenger. And because the Book surpasses the Sunnah in its wording, so it is not unclear that it is fit to be an abrogator. As for the Sunnah: only the ruling of the Book is abrogated by it, not its wording, and the Sunnah regarding the ruling is absolute revelation, making obligatory what the Book makes obligatory. So when the wording of the Book remains and its ruling is abrogated by the Sunnah, the abrogated becomes like the abrogator, inevitably. And if objection were lodged with the like of this, then that would not be valid regarding the Book being abrogated by the Book and the Sunnah by the Sunnah; rather, in that is the elevation of the station of the Messenger of Allah and the glorification of his Sunnah. And Allah knows best. And it becomes clear that it is not alteration from his own opinion, because Allah Almighty said: {Nor does he speak from [his own] desire} [53:3]. And it has reached us that when Allah revealed that they must return to the polytheists what they spent on those who emigrated from among their wives, and He ruled upon the Muslims: {And do not hold fast to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women}, that [the case of] Qariba bint Abi Umayya and the daughter of Jarwal al-Khuza'i occurred: Muawiya married Qariba, and Abu Jham married the other. When the disbelievers refused to acknowledge paying what the Muslims had spent on their wives, Allah revealed: {And if you have missed something of your wives from the disbelievers and you have retaliated}, and 'retaliation' means what the Muslims pay to the one whose wife has emigrated from the disbelievers, so he commanded that the one whose wife from among the Muslims had gone be given what he had spent as dowry from the women of the disbelievers who emigrated. And we do not know that any of the emigrant women apostatized after her faith. As for the hadith: it is evidence that the Book may abrogate the Sunnah. And the interpretation of the hadith [about presenting to the Book] is that presenting to the Book is only required regarding what is problematic in its date, or [what] is not in [a state of] authenticity such that the Book abrogates it, so giving precedence to the Book is more appropriate. As for His saying, Exalted is He: {We will bring something better than it or similar} [2:106]: the intended meaning of 'better' is in what relates to the benefit of the servants, not the wording by its meaning; so likewise is the similarity. However, we have clarified that the abrogation of the ruling of the Book by the Sunnah is outside this generality. And the abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah: like the Prophet's saying: 'I had prohibited you from visiting graves; but now visit them, for Muhammad has been permitted to visit his mother's grave. And I had prohibited you from keeping the meat of sacrificial animals for more than three days; now keep them as long as you wish. And I had prohibited you from (making) nabidh in gourds, green jars, hollowed-out stumps, and varnished vessels; now drink from any vessel, for the vessel does not make anything lawful nor unlawful.' And the abrogation of a solitary hadith by its like is also permissible. From Ibn Burayda from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'I had prohibited you from visiting graves, so visit them. And I had prohibited you from the meat of sacrificial animals for more than three days, so keep them as long as you wish. And I had prohibited you from nabidh except in a water-skin; so drink from any vessel, but do not drink anything intoxicating.' Narrated by Muslim. And al-Tirmidhi narrated from him: The Messenger of Allah said: 'I had prohibited you from visiting graves; now Muhammad has been permitted to visit his mother's grave. So visit them, for they remind of the Hereafter.'
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the permissibility of abrogation (naskh) between the Quran and the Sunnah. The author begins by presenting a rational proof: abrogation is merely a clarification of the duration of a ruling, and since the Prophet was sent as an explainer, he may clarify the Book's ruling. Moreover, the Quran's wording is superior to the Sunnah, so it can abrogate the Sunnah. Conversely, the Sunnah can abrogate a ruling of the Quran without affecting its wording, because the Sunnah in terms of ruling is also divine revelation. If this were not allowed, then abrogation of the Quran by the Quran and Sunnah by Sunnah would also be invalid, which is false. This upholds the status of the Sunnah. The verse 'Nor does he speak from desire' (53:3) confirms that the Prophet's speech is revelation, not personal opinion. The author then cites a historical example: when the verse about returning dowries to polytheists was revealed (60:10-11), some Muslim women emigrated, and the polytheists refused to pay compensation, so a later verse (60:11) provided a solution, showing that the Sunnah (the Prophet's practice) and subsequent revelation can interact. Next, the author argues from hadith that the Book can abrogate the Sunnah, interpreting the well-known command to 'present hadith to the Book' as applicable only to unclear or inauthentic reports. The verse 'We will bring something better or similar' (2:106) is explained as referring to benefit for the people, not the wording. Finally, examples of abrogation of Sunnah by Sunnah are given: the prohibition of grave-visiting was abrogated, the three-day limit on sacrificial meat was lifted, and the restriction on nabidh containers was removed. Solitary reports (khabar wahid) can also abrogate each other. Throughout, the author maintains the Hanafi position that all such forms of abrogation are valid.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: the lifting of a Sharia ruling by a later evidence, indicating the end of its duration.
السنة (al-Sunnah): The sayings, actions, and approvals of the Prophet, considered a source of law.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof in the passage, what is abrogation?
A) Alteration of the Quranic text
B) Clarification of the duration of a ruling
C) Complete nullification of a verse
D) Changing the wording of the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah, as divine revelation, can abrogate a Quranic ruling without altering its wording, by clarifying the duration of the ruling.

Naskh — Abrogation

Textual Evidences and Examples of Abrogation Between Quran and Sunnah
Textual evidence for cross-abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the specific hadith and historical examples used to demonstrate cross-abrogation and within-Sunnah abrogation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice and the Quranic story of the wives illustrate how abrogation occurs in practice between revelation sources.

This lesson examines the textual proofs and historical examples cited in the passage to support the permissibility of abrogation between the Quran and Sunnah. The story of the emigrant wives and the hadith about visiting graves, sacrificial meat, and nabidh containers provide concrete cases.

Guided Path
1
Examine the historical case of the wives
The case of Qariba and the daughter of Jarwal shows how a Quranic ruling (returning dowries) was later modified by another Quranic verse (60:11) in response to events, demonstrating that the Sunnah (the Prophet's action) and later revelation interact.
This is actually abrogation within the Quran, but the passage uses it to show the dynamic nature of revelation.
2
Analyze the hadith about presenting to the Book
Understand that the command to present hadith to the Quran is only for unclear or inauthentic reports, not for authentic sahih hadith.
3
Identify examples of Sunnah abrogating Sunnah
The hadith about visiting graves, sacrificial meat, and nabidh containers show the Prophet himself abrogating his earlier prohibitions.
4
Note the permissibility of khabar wahid abrogating another khabar wahid
The duplicate hadith from Ibn Burayda shows that even solitary reports can be abrogated by their like.

In the hadith about nabidh, what is abrogated?
A) The prohibition of nabidh entirely
